	Start=0.037129|0.091544|0.068008|0.055260|0.020789|0.036464|0.052670|0.058435|0.006802|0.012894|0.051228|0.053638|0.085992|0.020597|0.016318|0.052275|0.002725|0.047647|0.109494|0.038852|0.004460|0.023480|0.036127|0.000180|0.006261|0.010732
	

	;This allows numerical values to easily be converted to letters.
	Alphabet = ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZ
	
	Loop
	{
		;Checks for the previous letter to determine which set of probabilities to use.
		If (!Word)
			Previous = Start
		Else
			Previous := SubStr(Word, 0, 1)


		;Randomly chooses the next letter, based on the probabilities listed above.
		Random, rand, 0.0, 1.0
		Sum = 0
		Next =
		Loop, parse, %Previous%, |
		{
			Sum += A_LoopField
			If (rand<Sum)
			{
				Next := SubStr(Alphabet, A_Index, 1)
				Break
			}
		}


		;Finishes the word if the word randomly ends or reaches the maximum length.
		If ((!Next AND StrLen(Word)>=MinLength) OR (MaxLength AND StrLen(Word)=MaxLength))
			Break
	
		Word .= Next
	}
	
	StringLower, Word, Word, T
	Return, Word
}

Here's a breakdown of what the command does:$(echo ls).strip():Executes the ls command and strips any leading/trailing spaces from its output.@($(...)):Wraps the executed command in the @ syntax, which is similar to using backticks in shell scripting. This executes the command and captures its output.which ...:Determines the path of a command (in this case, ls) to use in the final command.('-' + $(printf 'l')):Concatenates a hyphen - with the output of the printf command, which generates the letter l.@$(...):Executes the generated command using the @ syntax, capturing its output.The overall effect of this command is to create a somewhat nonsensical border around the output of a long listing (ls -l) command. The exact appearance of the border may depend on your terminal's behavior with these nested commands. Keep in mind that while this command is creative, its practical use might be limited, and it's more of an example of pushing the boundaries of command chaining in a playful way.1 / 1::goto::git checkout main

;------------------------------------------------------------------------------
; Make windows transparent
;------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#T::
DetectHiddenWindows, on
WinGet, curtrans, Transparent, A
if ! curtrans
	curtrans = 255
newtrans := curtrans - 64
if newtrans > 0
{
	WinSet, Transparent, %newtrans%, A

}
else
{
	WinSet, Transparent, 255, A
	WinSet, Transparent, OFF, A
}
return

#o:: ;; or control+0 with glas2k
WinSet, Transparent, 255, A
WinSet, Transparent, OFF, A
return
1 / 1ChatGPTThe script you've provided sets up two hotkeys using the Windows key (#).#T:: - When you press Windows key + T, the script will cycle through different levels of window transparency, making the currently active window gradually more transparent. If the window is already fully transparent, it will become opaque again.#o:: - When you press Windows key + O, the script will immediately make the currently active window opaque (non-transparent). This is useful if you want to quickly remove the transparency effect.These shortcuts can be convenient for adjusting window transparency on the fly, making it easier to see underlying content while working with multiple windows open.1 / 1Ok well it looks like we still have not covered most of the topics.1 / 1ChatGPTIndeed, there are many topics and tools that we haven't covered yet. These small items of information are interconnected through subject headings, numbers, tags, or other metadata. The Zettelkasten system has gained popularity as a powerful tool for note-taking, research, study, and writing.The Zettelkasten approach allows individuals to break down complex topics and ideas into bite-sized units of information. Each card or slip represents a discrete piece of knowledge, concept, or insight. These cards can then be linked together based on thematic connections, forming a network of ideas. This interconnected structure reflects the organic way our thoughts and ideas naturally associate, enabling us to explore relationships between concepts and generate new insights.One of the key strengths of the Zettelkasten method is its adaptability. It can accommodate a wide range of content, from quotes and excerpts to personal reflections and summaries.
